    <h1 style="color: cadetblue;" align="center">List of my favorite books</h1>
    <p style="color: rgb(95, 158, 160);"" align="center">
      (These are some books I read recently or will read soon)
    </p>
    <div>
      <br />
      <ol>
        <li>
          <a href="https://www.al-islam.org/quran/" target="_blank">Al Quran</a>
        </li>
        <p> <strong> <em>
          "The Quran" is the holy book of Islam, believed by Muslims to be the
          word of God as revealed to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him)
          over a period of 23 years. It consists of 114 chapters, or surahs,
          which are organized by length rather than chronology. The Quran covers
          a range of topics, including the oneness of God, the prophethood of
          Muhammad, the stories of past prophets and civilizations, moral
          guidance, laws and regulations, and the afterlife. It is considered
          the ultimate authority in Islamic theology and jurisprudence, and is
          revered by Muslims as a source of spiritual guidance, inspiration, and
          wisdom. The Quran is written in Arabic and is recited and memorized by
          Muslims around the world as an act of worship and devotion
        </p> </strong> </em> <br> 
        <li>
          <a
            href="https://www.amazon.com/Ar-Raheeq-Al-Makhtum-Sealed-Nectar-Biography/dp/1591440718"
            target="_blank"
            >Ar Raheeq Al Makhtum</a
          >
        </li>
        <p> <strong> <em>
          "Ar-Raheeq Al-Makhtum" is a book that narrates the life of the Prophet
          Muhammad (peace be upon him) in great detail. The book, written by
          Safiur Rahman Mubarakpuri, is a comprehensive biography that covers
          the Prophet's life from his birth to his death. It highlights the key
          events and milestones in the Prophet's life, including his early years
          in Mecca, his migration to Medina, the battles he fought, and the
          treaties he made. The book also delves into the Prophet's character,
          his teachings, and his interactions with his companions, family, and
          enemies. "Ar-Raheeq Al-Makhtum" is widely regarded as one of the most
          authentic and reliable sources of information on the life of the
          Prophet Muhammad, and is used as a reference by scholars, researchers,
          and students of Islamic history and theology
        </p> </strong> </em>
        <br>
        <li>
          <a
            href="https://www.goodreads.com/en/book/show/18144590"
            target="_blank"
            >The Alchemist</a
          >
        </li>
        <p> <strong> <em>
          "The Alchemist" is a novel written by Brazilian author Paulo Coelho.
          It tells the story of Santiago, a shepherd boy from Spain who embarks
          on a journey to fulfill his dreams and find his purpose in life. Along
          the way, he meets a series of characters who help him understand the
          importance of following one's heart and pursuing one's personal
          legend. The novel is a blend of adventure, spirituality, and
          philosophy. It explores themes such as the pursuit of dreams, the
          power of the universe, and the importance of listening to one's inner
          voice. The story is set in exotic locations such as Andalusia, the
          Sahara Desert, and the Pyramids of Egypt, which add to the mystical
          and enchanting atmosphere of the novel. "The Alchemist" has been
          widely popular since its publication in 1988 and has been translated
          into over 80 languages. It has sold over 65 million copies worldwide
          and is considered a modern classic. The novel has inspired readers
          around the world to follow their dreams and pursue their passions, and
          has become a source of inspiration and motivation for many
        </p> </strong> </em> <br>
        <li>
          <a
            href="https://www.cambridge.org/us/cambridgeenglish/campaigns/inuse">
            English Grammar In Use</a
          >
        </li>
        <p> <strong> <em>
          "English Grammar in Use" is a popular English language textbook
          written by Raymond Murphy. It is designed to help learners of English,
          particularly those at the intermediate level, to improve their grammar
          skills and develop their ability to communicate effectively in
          English. The book is divided into units, each of which focuses on a
          specific aspect of English grammar, such as verb tenses, articles, and
          prepositions. Each unit contains explanations of the grammar rules,
          followed by a variety of exercises to help learners practice and
          reinforce their understanding of the material. The exercises include
          fill-in-the-blank, multiple choice, and error correction tasks, as
          well as writing and speaking activities. "English Grammar in Use" is
          widely used by teachers and students of English as a second language
          around the world. It is known for its clear and concise explanations,
          its comprehensive coverage of English grammar, and its practical
          approach to teaching grammar in context. The book also includes a
          handy reference section at the back, which provides a summary of the
          grammar rules covered in the book, as well as a list of irregular
          verbs and other useful information for learners of English
        </p> </strong> </em>
        <br>
        <li>
          <a
            href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153747.Moby_Dick_or_the_Whale"
            target="_blank"
            >Moby Dick</a
          >
        </li>
        <p> <strong> <em>
          "Moby-Dick" is a novel written by American author Herman Melville,
          first published in 1851. It tells the story of a sailor named Ishmael
          and his obsession with the elusive and vengeful white whale,
          Moby-Dick. The novel explores themes such as obsession, revenge, fate,
          and the struggle between man and nature. The story is set on board the
          whaling ship Pequod, captained by the enigmatic and tyrannical Ahab,
          who has a personal vendetta against Moby-Dick. As the ship sets sail
          on a dangerous and treacherous voyage, Ishmael and the other crew
          members must navigate their way through the perils of the sea and the
          madness of their captain. "Moby-Dick" is known for its rich and
          complex symbolism, vivid descriptions of whaling and life at sea, and
          its philosophical and metaphysical themes. The novel also includes
          digressions on a variety of topics, such as whale anatomy, cetology,
          and the history of whaling, which add depth and richness to the
          narrative. Despite its mixed critical reception when it was first
          published, "Moby-Dick" is now considered one of the greatest American
          novels and a masterpiece of world literature. It has been adapted into
          numerous films, plays, and other works of art and continues to
          captivate readers with its timeless themes and powerful storytelling
        </p> </strong> </em>
        <br>
      </ol>

It explores the nature of the human mind and its functioning.YouYou Know How When You Learn a New Word, You See It Everywhere? Science Knows Why
HUMANS
24 March 2016
ByJOSH HRALA

(Alastair Bennett/Flickr)
Have you ever learned a new word, one that you swear you've never heard before, only to find it popping up throughout your daily life for a few days after? It's like the word is haunting you, or that the word didn't exist at all before you learned it. Well, turns out that's called the Baader-Meinhof phenomenon, and it all comes down to your brain playing tricks on you.ChatGPTChatGPTThe Baader-Meinhof phenomenon, also known as the frequency illusion or Haunted People Syndrome, is a cognitive bias that leads people to notice a certain phrase, idea, or object more frequently once it has been brought to their attention. This phenomenon was named in 1994 after an individual noticed repeated references to the Baader-Meinhof group following a single mention. The illusion is primarily driven by two psychological processes: selective attention and confirmation bias.Selective Attention: This is the process of focusing on relevant stimuli while ignoring distractions, leading people to unconsciously filter information relevant to themââ.Confirmation Bias: This bias involves seeking evidence that confirms one's beliefs or hypotheses, often overlooking contrary evidence. In the context of the Baader-Meinhof phenomenon, once an individual starts noticing a specific stimulus, they focus on it more, reinforcing their belief in its increased frequency even though its actual frequency hasn't changedââ.These cognitive processes work together to create the impression that a newly learned word or concept is suddenly appearing everywhereââ.YouI wonder if there is a word for when you say something outloud and then you see it everywhereChatGPTChatGPTThe term you're referring to is similar to the Baader-Meinhof phenomenon, also known as the frequency illusion. This cognitive bias describes the experience where once something comes to your attention, you start noticing it everywhere. However, there doesn't appear to be a specific term for when this occurs specifically after saying something out loud. The underlying principle is the same: once your attention is drawn to something, whether by hearing, reading, or saying it, your brain is more likely to notice it in the future.YouWhat about when you say something outloud and then other people see it and bring it to you?ChatGPTChatGPTThe scenario you're describing, where you say something out loud and then others notice it and bring it to your attention, doesn't have a specific, widely-recognized term like the Baader-Meinhof phenomenon. However, it can be seen as a combination of a few psychological and social phenomena:Selective Attention and Confirmation Bias: As in the Baader-Meinhof phenomenon, once a topic is mentioned, people are more likely to notice related information due to selective attention. If they are aware that the topic is of interest to you, confirmation bias might make them more likely to bring it to your attention.Social Sharing of Attention: This occurs when a topic or item of interest is shared within a social group, making it more noticeable to the group members. When you mention something, it becomes a shared point of focus, leading others to recognize and bring up related information.Information Cascades: This is a social phenomenon where people follow the actions or opinions of others. In this case, mentioning something out loud can set off a chain reaction where others, picking up on your interest, start paying more attention to that topic themselves.While there isn't a single term that encapsulates this entire process, it's an interplay of attention, social dynamics, and cognitive biases.YouI mentioned two two people both of which brought me some or said they they would, I was talking about old continuous computer paper with the perforationsChatGPTChatGPTThe situation you experienced, where you mentioned old continuous computer paper with perforations and then two people subsequently brought it up or offered it to you, aligns well with the concept of priming in psychology, combined with elements of social interaction and attentiveness.Priming: This is a psychological phenomenon where exposure to one stimulus influences the response to another stimulus. By mentioning the continuous computer paper, you may have primed the individuals you were speaking with to be more aware of this item. This increased awareness could make them more likely to notice it or think about it in their surroundings.Social Responsiveness: In social interactions, people often want to be helpful or relevant. When you mentioned an interest or need, these individuals might have been motivated to respond in a helpful manner, either by bringing you the item or planning to do so.Selective Perception: Similar to selective attention, this is where individuals subconsciously filter and respond to information that is relevant to their current interests or concerns. Your mention of the paper possibly triggered a selective perception in these individuals, making them more attentive to this specific item.In summary, by mentioning the continuous computer paper, you likely influenced the attention and behavior of the people you were talking to, leading them to notice and respond to this item more than they would have otherwise.YouAnd then I'm installing dispensers in a washroom in an airport hanger and I stack a foot and a half long shoved under a sink in the workers repair room with a stack of national geographics dating from the seventiesChatGPTChatGPTIt sounds like you experienced a rather unique and serendipitous event! This could be an example of what's often called a "synchronicity" â a concept introduced by psychologist Carl Jung, which refers to meaningful coincidences that seem to have no causal relationship but are meaningfully related.In your case, the key elements are:Synchronicity: The seemingly unrelated event of installing dispensers in an airport hangar washroom leading to the discovery of vintage magazines aligns with Jung's concept of synchronicity. This concept suggests that these occurrences are not just coincidences but have some form of meaningful connection, even if it's not immediately apparent.Serendipity: This refers to finding something good without looking for it. While you were working in a seemingly unrelated setting, you stumbled upon a collection of old magazines, which can be seen as a serendipitous discovery, especially considering your recent conversation about old continuous computer paper.Contextual Rarity: Finding such items in a unique and unexpected setting like an airport hangar repair room adds an element of surprise and rarity to the discovery.While there's no direct causal link between your conversation about old continuous computer paper and finding vintage National Geographic magazines, the timing and context make it a noteworthy coincidence. SURFACES AND INTERFACES RESEARCH UPDATE
Did slippery sand help Egyptians build the pyramids?
06 May 2014 Hamish Johnston

Slip-sliding away in ancient Egypt
Workers building the colossal monuments of ancient Egypt may have added water to the desert sands to make it easier to haul giant sledges. That is the conclusion of an international team of physicists that studied the relationship between friction and water content in a number of different types of sand. The research suggests that the type of sand found in the Egyptian desert becomes particularly slippery when wet â something that might have made it much easier to move the huge stones that were used to build the pyramids.

The study was done by Christian Wagner and colleagues at Saarland University in Germany, along with researchers in the Netherlands, Iran and France. The team was inspired by an ancient Egyptian wall painting showing a huge statue being hauled across the sand on a sledge in about 1800 BC. The painting has a detail that has long puzzled Egyptologists: a worker who appears to be pouring water onto the sand in front of the sledge while others appear to be carrying water to replenish his supply.

Ritual or lubrication?
While some historians believe that the act of pouring a liquid could be some sort of ritual, Wagner and colleagues wondered if it was a practical measure to reduce friction between the sledge and sand. This thought was inspired by work done in 2007 by Wagner, along with his Saarland colleague Jorge Fiscina, who showed that just a small amount of water acts as a lubricant that reduces friction in sand that is being pushed through a tube (see âWet sand flows better than dryâ).

To test their new theory, Wagner, Fiscina and colleagues measured the resistance experienced by a sledge being dragged through different types of sand. The teamâs sledge was made from PVC, measured 11 Ã 7.5 cm and had rounded edges to mimic its ancient counterparts. It was loaded with heavy weights so that it exerted a downward force of about 250 kg/m2, which is on a par with that of a loaded Egyptian sledge. The sledge was pulled by a tensile tester, which measured the force required to move the sledge and allowed the team to calculate the coefficient of dynamic friction. While the researchers found that the addition of water did indeed reduce friction, it was not because the water allowed the sand to flow more freely â indeed, it had the opposite effect.

Concrete-like surface
The team quickly realized that sand piling up in front of the sledge was a major contributor to the friction. When the sand is dry or slightly damp, the grains can move past each other and are easily pushed up into a pile that makes it harder to pull the sledge. As more water is added to the sand, however, the grains begin to stick together and eventually form a stiff concrete-like surface that the sledge can slide across much more easily than across dry sand. This stickiness between grains was also observed in Wagnerâs 2007 study, where it impeded the flow of sand.

In the case of one type of sand tested, the coefficient of dynamic friction nearly halved when the water content of the sand reached about 5%. This sand is similar to that found in Egypt, suggesting that wetting the sand would have been a boon to ancient monument builders. The results also indicate that the pyramid builders had luck on their side. Egyptian sand is âpolydispersiveâ, which means that it contains grains of many different sizes. When Wagner and colleagues used sand in which most grains were of a certain size, the drop in friction was much less than that seen in the Egyptian-like sand. This could be because the range of grain sizes in polydispersive sand allows it to pack more tightly than sand where most grains are the same size.

More water does not help
Another important finding by the team is that above 5% water content, friction increased as more water was added. In some cases, friction on sand with 10% water content actually surpassed the value measured for dry sand. Wagner told physicsworld.com that the reason for this increase was not clear because the researchers did not see heaps of wet sand piling up in front of the sledge. Instead, he speculates that wetter sand is softer than the concrete-like sand and so the sledge sinks into it. âMaybe it is a bit like the difference between sliding on concrete and sliding on rubber,â says Wagner. âIn any case, this is something we have to investigate in future studies.â

Troy Shinbrot of Rutgers University described the results of the experiment as âcompellingâ but points out that more work needs to be done to understand the connections between friction and the stiffness of the sand. As for practical applications beyond building pyramids, Shinbrot points out that the research could help us to understand the effects of moisture on processing a range of granular materials from pharmaceuticals to industrial slurries.

The experiments are described in Physical Review Letters.

ChatGPTChatGPTThe article titled "Did slippery sand help Egyptians build the pyramids?" by Hamish Johnston, published on May 6, 2014, provides an intriguing perspective on the construction of the ancient Egyptian pyramids. The key points from this article are:Research on Friction and Water Content in Sand: A team of physicists, led by Christian Wagner at Saarland University in Germany, conducted research to understand the relationship between friction and water content in different types of sand.Inspiration from Ancient Egyptian Wall Painting: The team was inspired by a wall painting from around 1800 BC, showing a large statue being transported across the desert on a sledge, with a worker pouring water in front of it.Hypothesis of Reducing Friction: Contrary to the belief that the act of pouring water was a ritual, the researchers proposed that it was a practical measure to reduce the friction between the sledge and the sand.Experimental Findings: The experiments showed that a small amount of water (about 5% water content) added to the sand significantly reduced friction. This was not because the water made the sand flow more freely but because it caused the sand grains to stick together, forming a stiffer surface easier for sledges to slide over.Importance of Sand Type: The type of sand found in the Egyptian desert, which is polydispersive (contains grains of many different sizes), was particularly effective at reducing friction when wet. This property was fortuitous for the ancient Egyptians in their monument-building efforts.Limit to Water's Effectiveness: Adding more than 5% water actually increased friction, potentially because the wetter sand was softer and caused the sledge to sink into it.Broader Implications: Beyond pyramid building, the study's results could have implications for understanding the effects of moisture on processing various granular materials in modern industries.This research offers a scientific explanation for a long-standing historical mystery and showcases the ingenious methods that might have been employed by the ancient Egyptians in constructing their monumental structures.YouI forgot to mention that the material in question was sandChatGPTChatGPTThe research discussed in the article by Hamish Johnston indeed focuses on the properties of sand, specifically how ancient Egyptians might have used water to alter its properties for the construction of the pyramids. The key findings from this research, which are particularly relevant given that the material in question is sand, include:Sand's Behavior with Water: The study revealed that the frictional properties of sand change significantly when a small amount of water is added. This is particularly relevant to the type of sand found in the Egyptian desert.Creating a Concrete-like Surface: By adding water to the sand, the grains begin to stick together, forming a stiffer, concrete-like surface. This surface would be easier for sledges to slide over, compared to dry sand.Optimal Water Content: The researchers found that about 5% water content in the sand was optimal for reducing friction. More water than this would increase friction, making it harder to pull the sledges.Polydispersive Sand's Advantage: Egyptian sand's polydispersive nature, containing grains of many different sizes, played a crucial role. This type of sand packs more tightly than sand with uniform grain size, making it more effective at reducing friction when wet.Real-World Application: Beyond the historical context of pyramid building, this research could inform current industrial practices involving granular materials.This study offers a fascinating look at how a seemingly simple substance like sand can have complex properties that the ancient Egyptians might have ingeniously exploited to their advantage in monumental construction tasks.YouSo give my Bread Beer theory in outlineChatGPTChatGPTYour Bread Beer theory, as it relates to the construction of the Egyptian pyramids, can be outlined as follows:Bread Beer Theory Outline1.
